**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. ### **Area 1: The Epstein Investigation & Political Fallout**

The scandal surrounding Jeffrey Epstein has rapidly intensified into a dominant national crisis, directly implicating the President and his inner circle and triggering a multi-front response from the White House, Congress, and the media. The crisis ignited with the publication of a *Wall Street Journal* exposé, which multiple sources allege President Trump and his team actively attempted to block or censor [1, 2]. The story's central claim is that a birthday letter sent to Epstein "bore Trump’s signature, drawing of naked woman" [3]. While most reports focus on this letter, another specifies the President contributed to an "album for Epstein’s 50th Birthday" [4]. The President has issued a public response to the report concerning the letter [5]. Adding to the severity of the situation, a former casino executive has made a separate, direct allegation that Trump and Epstein, whom he described as "best friends," were once "caught bringing underage girls to a casino floor" [6].

The administration’s reaction has been twofold: an aggressive counter-offensive against the media and a simultaneous move toward selective transparency. President Trump has publicly threatened to sue the *Wall Street Journal* for its story [7], and one report describes his team as having been on a “‘F-cking Warpath’ to Kill" the exposé before its publication [8]. In a parallel action, the President has directed Attorney General Pam Bondi to seek the public release of grand jury testimony and transcripts from the original Epstein case [9, 10]. This directive is framed by at least one international outlet as a direct response to mounting public pressure [11]. However, this overture towards transparency is contrasted by the White House’s stated opposition to appointing a special prosecutor to investigate the matter further [12].

Congressional oversight is intensifying and exposing partisan and intra-party fault lines. The controversy is also creating significant political challenges for the House GOP leadership, with Speaker Mike Johnson reportedly forced to react to "Republican blowback" over the scandal [14]. The media environment remains saturated with new information and speculation. ABC News reports that unreleased Epstein files "include logbooks for private island" [15], while the New York Times has characterized the drip of information as a "perfect recipe for conspiracy theories" [16]. Public reaction is fractured, with reports that "MAGA world" has leaped to the President’s defense [17], while prominent figures offer starkly different takes. Elon Musk has publicly mocked the issue as an "'Epstein hoax'," while former Speaker Nancy Pelosi has dismissed the entire controversy as "a distraction" [18, 19].

### **Area 3: Domestic Policy and Governance**

### **Area 4: Congressional Activity & Political Landscape**

Congress has advanced major legislation this week, though legislative action has been marked by political turmoil and revealed sharp intra-party tensions. The House gave final approval to a signature Trump priority: a "$9 billion cut to public broadcasting and foreign aid" [1], sending the package to the President's desk after a late-night vote [2]. The bill specifically defunds programs at PBS, NPR, and USAID [3]. The bill's path was not smooth; its consideration was delayed by the Epstein controversy [4], and it exposed fissures within the GOP, with some Republican members publicly airing "concerns about Trump’s use of rare tool to cut funds despite backing bill" [5]. Following its passage, Vice President JD Vance has been publicly promoting the "Benefits of Trump’s Megabill but Ignores the Costs," according to a New York Times analysis [6].

In a notable display of bipartisanship, a major crypto regulation bill was sent to the President's desk with significant support from the opposition, as "102 House Democrats, Including Jeffries," joined the GOP to pass the measure [7]. This cooperation stands in stark contrast to deepening party divisions. Reports cite ongoing "infighting among U.S. House Republicans" [8], exemplified by Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene taking aim at the very same crypto bill backed by President Trump, thus deepening the split [9]. In response to the political environment, Democrats are reportedly adopting a new communications strategy that is "Less scripted, more cursing, Trumpier insults" in an effort to project an authenticity they feel voters associate with Trump [10]. The political climate has grown increasingly personal, highlighted by a report of two congressmen engaging in a "Jaw-Dropping Battle on Live TV" [11].

### **Area 5: Economic & Financial Policy**

A direct and public conflict has surfaced between the Federal Reserve and the Executive Branch over fiscal management and institutional autonomy. Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell has publicly defended a "$2.5 billion Fed renovation" project, issuing what was characterized as a detailed "point-by-point response to the Trump administration," signaling a significant and open disagreement over the independent central bank's authority [1].

In international trade, high-stakes negotiations with Canada are "back underway." On the domestic front, a recent Federal Reserve report concludes that the economic effects of current trade policy are being more widely felt, as American businesses are now "passing along tariff costs" to consumers [3].

In financial sector regulation, the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) is reportedly considering new frameworks for digital assets. According to a Bloomberg headline, the SEC is set to "Weigh ‘Innovation Exception’ Tied to Crypto." This suggestion is attributed to an individual named Atkins, though no further details on their role or the specifics of the proposal are available in the provided headlines [4].

### **Area 1: The Epstein Investigation & Political Fallout**

The scandal surrounding Jeffrey Epstein has escalated into the dominant national crisis, directly implicating President Trump and his inner circle. The situation has prompted a multi-front response involving an aggressive media counter-offensive from the White House, intensifying congressional oversight, and fractured public reaction. The crisis ignited after the *Wall Street Journal* published an exposé that, according to multiple reports, the President's team had actively attempted to block or censor [1, 2]. The story’s central claim is that a birthday letter sent to Jeffrey Epstein "bore Trump’s signature, drawing of naked woman" [3]. Another report specifies the President contributed to an "album for Epstein’s 50th Birthday" [4]. The President has since issued a public response to the letter report [5]. Compounding the issue, a former casino executive has made a separate, direct allegation that Trump and Epstein, whom the executive called "best friends," were once "caught bringing underage girls to a casino floor" [6].

The administration’s reaction has been twofold: an aggressive campaign against the media and a simultaneous move toward selective transparency. President Trump has publicly threatened to sue the *Wall Street Journal* [7], while one report describes his team as having been on a “‘F-cking Warpath’ to Kill” the story before its publication [8]. In a parallel action, the President has directed Attorney General Pam Bondi to seek the public release of grand jury testimony and transcripts from the original Epstein case [9, 10]. This directive is framed by at least one international outlet as a direct response to mounting public pressure [11]. However, this overture is contrasted by the White House’s stated opposition to appointing a special prosecutor to investigate the matter further [12].

Congressional oversight is intensifying and exposing political fault lines. The Senate Finance Committee, chaired by Ron Wyden (D-OR), has unveiled details of what it calls "Treasury’s Undisclosed Epstein File," accusing the Trump administration of sitting on Epstein-related bank records and "refusing to investigate" [13]. The controversy is also creating significant political challenges for House leadership, with Speaker Mike Johnson reportedly forced to react to "Republican blowback" [14]. The media environment remains saturated, with ABC News reporting that unreleased Epstein files "include logbooks for private island" [15] and others noting the situation is a "perfect recipe for conspiracy theories" [16]. Public reaction is sharply divided. Reports indicate "MAGA world" has leaped to the President’s defense [17], while prominent figures offer starkly different takes. Elon Musk has publicly mocked the issue as an "'Epstein hoax'," while former Speaker Nancy Pelosi has dismissed the entire controversy as "a distraction" [18, 19].

### **Area 2: Foreign Affairs & National Security**

The administration’s national security apparatus is being reshaped by disruptive personnel changes at the State Department. Recent layoffs have reportedly cut "deeper than previously known" and have specifically targeted "personnel involved in cyber, quantum, AI and tech-focused roles" [1]. An Associated Press report confirms these reductions directly affect a range of President Trump's key foreign policy priorities, including "intelligence, energy and China" [2].

Simultaneously, diplomatic frictions are visible across several key bilateral relationships. In the Middle East, the Israeli government publicly declared a deadly strike on a Gaza church was a "mistake" only after receiving a phone call from President Trump on the matter [3]. Tensions with Brazil are openly escalating, with President Lula da Silva quoted as saying President Trump was “‘not elected to be emperor of the world’” [4]. To the north, a PBS report indicates that Canadian tourism to the U.S. has dropped dramatically, a decline attributed to what the report calls President Trump's "harsh rhetoric" [5].

A distinct international human rights concern has been raised by The Guardian. The report alleges that migrants who have been deported by the United States to the nation of Eswatini are "being held in solitary confinement" [6]. The provided headlines offer no further context on the scale or specifics of this situation.

### **Area 3: Domestic Policy and Governance**

The administration is actively pursuing its domestic agenda through significant deregulatory actions, budget cuts, and new enforcement protocols. On environmental and energy policy, the state of Louisiana has canceled a "$3 billion coastal restoration project" that was funded by a settlement from a major oil spill [1]. This action coincides with reports that the Trump administration is broadly exempting "Scores of Plants From Biden’s Pollution Rules" [2]. Federal resource management has also drawn public criticism, with one report questioning "Why the Trump Administration Is About to Set Fire to 500 Tons of Emergency Food" [3], and another highlighting actor Nick Offerman's sharp rebuke of the administration for cutting "$267 Million From National Parks Budget," a move he termed “‘S—ting the Bed’” [4].

In justice and immigration policy, new data-sharing agreements and enforcement tactics are being implemented. A report alleges that Medicaid is now providing Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) access to the personal data of "79M Enrollees, Including Ethnicity" [5]. In terms of detention, advocates claim migrants at a Louisiana facility dubbed 'Alligator Alcatraz' are being systematically prevented from accessing legal counsel [6]. At a local level, an ICE arrest of a chiropractor "outside his kid’s Beaverton preschool" in Oregon has drawn media attention [7].

On social policy and election law, the government of Puerto Rico has enacted a ban on "hormone therapy and gender surgery for trans people under 21" [8]. Separately, the Republican National Committee (RNC) has filed a lawsuit in New Jersey demanding "Access to Voter Roll and Election Machine Records" [9]. Adding a symbolic dimension to law-and-order rhetoric, Attorney General Pam Bondi recently visited Alcatraz after President Trump floated the "idea of reopening the former federal prison" [10]. Public perception of these policies is negative, according to a single survey reported by The Hill, which finds, "Most say Trump policies haven't helped them" [11].

### **Area 4: Congressional Activity & Political Landscape**

Congress has advanced major legislation this week, though legislative action has been marked by political turmoil and revealed sharp intra-party tensions. The House gave final approval to a signature Trump priority: a "$9 billion cut to public broadcasting and foreign aid" [1], sending the package to the President's desk after a late-night vote [2]. The bill specifically defunds programs at PBS, NPR, and USAID [3]. The bill's path was not smooth; its consideration was delayed by the Epstein controversy [4], and it exposed fissures within the GOP, with some Republican members publicly airing "concerns about Trump’s use of rare tool to cut funds despite backing bill" [5]. Following its passage, Vice President JD Vance has been publicly promoting the "Benefits of Trump’s Megabill but Ignores the Costs," according to a New York Times analysis [6].

In a notable display of bipartisanship, a major crypto regulation bill was sent to the President's desk with significant support from the opposition, as "102 House Democrats, Including Jeffries," joined the GOP to pass the measure [7]. This cooperation stands in stark contrast to deepening party divisions. Reports cite ongoing "infighting among U.S. House Republicans" [8], exemplified by Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene taking aim at the very same crypto bill backed by President Trump, thus deepening the split [9]. In response to the political environment, Democrats are reportedly adopting a new communications strategy that is "Less scripted, more cursing, Trumpier insults" in an effort to project an authenticity they feel voters associate with Trump [10]. The political climate has grown increasingly personal, highlighted by a report of two congressmen engaging in a "Jaw-Dropping Battle on Live TV" [11].

### **Area 5: Economic & Financial Policy**

A direct and public conflict has surfaced between the Federal Reserve and the Executive Branch over fiscal management and institutional autonomy. Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell has publicly defended a "$2.5 billion Fed renovation" project, issuing what was characterized as a detailed "point-by-point response to the Trump administration," signaling a significant and open disagreement over the independent central bank's authority [1].

In international trade, high-stakes negotiations with Canada are "back underway." According to reports, President Trump's "wish list" for these talks is expanding to include a wide array of topics "from oil to DEI" policies, suggesting a broad and complex U.S. agenda [2]. On the domestic front, a recent Federal Reserve report concludes that the economic effects of current trade policy are being more widely felt, as American businesses are now "passing along tariff costs" to consumers [3].

In financial sector regulation, the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) is reportedly considering new frameworks for digital assets. According to a Bloomberg headline, the SEC is set to "Weigh ‘Innovation Exception’ Tied to Crypto." This suggestion is attributed to an individual named Atkins, though no further details on their role or the specifics of the proposal are available in the provided headlines [4].

## 3. Domestic Policy and Governance

The administration is actively pursuing its domestic agenda through significant deregulatory actions, budget cuts, and new enforcement protocols. On environmental and energy policy, the state of Louisiana has canceled a "$3 billion coastal restoration project" that was funded by a settlement from a major oil spill [1]. This action coincides with reports that the Trump administration is broadly exempting "Scores of Plants From Biden’s Pollution Rules" [2]. Federal resource management has also drawn public criticism, with one report questioning "Why the Trump Administration Is About to Set Fire to 500 Tons of Emergency Food" [3], and another highlighting actor Nick Offerman's sharp rebuke of the administration for cutting "$267 Million From National Parks Budget," a move he termed “‘S—ting the Bed’” [4].

In justice and immigration policy, new data-sharing agreements and enforcement tactics are being implemented. A report alleges that Medicaid is now providing Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) access to the personal data of "79M Enrollees, Including Ethnicity" [5]. In terms of detention, advocates claim migrants at a Louisiana facility dubbed 'Alligator Alcatraz' are being systematically prevented from accessing legal counsel [6]. At a local level, an ICE arrest of a chiropractor "outside his kid’s Beaverton preschool" in Oregon has drawn media attention [7].

On social policy and election law, the government of Puerto Rico has enacted a ban on "hormone therapy and gender surgery for trans people under 21" [8]. Separately, the Republican National Committee (RNC) has filed a lawsuit in New Jersey demanding "Access to Voter Roll and Election Machine Records" [9]. Adding a symbolic dimension to law-and-order rhetoric, Attorney General Pam Bondi recently visited Alcatraz after President Trump floated the "idea of reopening the former federal prison" [10]. Public perception of these policies is negative, according to a single survey reported by The Hill, which finds, "Most say Trump policies haven't helped them" [11].

## 4. Congressional Activity & Political Landscape

Congress has advanced major legislation this week, though legislative action has been marked by political turmoil and revealed sharp intra-party tensions. The House gave final approval to a signature Trump priority: a "$9 billion cut to public broadcasting and foreign aid" [1], sending the package to the President's desk after a late-night vote [2]. The bill specifically defunds programs at PBS, NPR, and USAID [3]. The bill's path was not smooth; its consideration was delayed by the Epstein controversy [4], and it exposed fissures within the GOP, with some Republican members publicly airing "concerns about Trump’s use of rare tool to cut funds despite backing bill" [5]. Following its passage, Vice President JD Vance has been publicly promoting the "Benefits of Trump’s Megabill but Ignores the Costs," according to a New York Times analysis [6].

In a notable display of bipartisanship, a major crypto regulation bill was sent to the President's desk with significant support from the opposition, as "102 House Democrats, Including Jeffries," joined the GOP to pass the measure [7]. This cooperation stands in stark contrast to deepening party divisions. Reports cite ongoing "infighting among U.S. House Republicans" [8], exemplified by Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene taking aim at the very same crypto bill backed by President Trump, thus deepening the split [9]. In response to the political environment, Democrats are reportedly adopting a new communications strategy that is "Less scripted, more cursing, Trumpier insults" in an effort to project an authenticity they feel voters associate with Trump [10]. The political climate has grown increasingly personal, highlighted by a report of two congressmen engaging in a "Jaw-Dropping Battle on Live TV" [11].

## 5. Economic & Financial Policy

A direct and public conflict has surfaced between the Federal Reserve and the Executive Branch over fiscal management and institutional autonomy. Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell has publicly defended a "$2.5 billion Fed renovation" project, issuing what was characterized as a detailed "point-by-point response to the Trump administration," signaling a significant and open disagreement over the independent central bank's authority [1].

In international trade, high-stakes negotiations with Canada are "back underway." According to reports, President Trump's "wish list" for these talks is expanding to include a wide array of topics "from oil to DEI" policies, suggesting a broad and complex U.S. agenda [2]. On the domestic front, a recent Federal Reserve report concludes that the economic effects of current trade policy are being more widely felt, as American businesses are now "passing along tariff costs" to consumers [3].

In financial sector regulation, the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) is reportedly considering new frameworks for digital assets. According to a Bloomberg headline, the SEC is set to "Weigh ‘Innovation Exception’ Tied to Crypto." This suggestion is attributed to an individual named Atkins, though no further details on their role or the specifics of the proposal are available in the provided headlines [4].
